We made it minimal because we will be offering this as a plugin for Salesforce, Lofty, Hubspot and others. Here is the file: import React, { createContext, useContext, useEffect, useState } from "react";
import { createClient } from "@supabase/supabase-js";

// Supabase Setup
const supabase = createClient(
  import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_URL!,
  import.meta.env.VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY!
);

// Contact Type
export interface Contact {
  id: string;
  user_id: string;
  name: string;
  email?: string;
  phone?: string;
  mailing_address?: string;
  status: "healthy" | "neglected" | "critical";
  urgency: number;
  last_contact_date?: string;
  contact_frequency_days?: number;
  notes?: string;
  tags?: string[];
  created_at: string;
}

// Theme Context
const ThemeContext = createContext({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: (theme: string) => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState("zombie");
  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);

// Views
import ZombieView from "./components/ZombieView";
import TreeView from "./components/TreeView";
import StarshipView from "./components/StarshipView";
import RingGatesView from "./components/RingGatesView";

// Contact Form Component
function ContactForm({ onAdd }: { onAdd: () => void }) {
  const [name, setName] = useState("");
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [phone, setPhone] = useState("");
  const [tags, setTags] = useState("");
  const [error, setError] = useState("");

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    setError("");

    const user = (await supabase.auth.getUser()).data.user;
    if (!user) {
      setError("Not logged in.");
      return;
    }

    const { error: insertError } = await supabase.from("contacts").insert({
      user_id: user.id,
      name,
      email,
      phone,
      tags: tags
        .split(",")
        .map((t) => t.trim())
        .filter((t) => t.length > 0),
      status: "healthy",
      urgency: 3,
    });

    if (insertError) {
      setError(insertError.message);
    } else {
      setName("");
      setEmail("");
      setPhone("");
      setTags("");
      onAdd();
    }
  };

  return (
    <form
      onSubmit={handleSubmit}
      className="bg-white shadow-md rounded-xl p-6 mb-6 space-y-4 border border-gray-200"
    >
      <h2 className="text-xl font-semibold mb-2 text-gray-800">
        Add New Contact
      </h2>
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Name"
        value={name}
        onChange={(e) => setName(e.target.value)}
        required
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Email"
        value={email}
        onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Phone"
        value={phone}
        onChange={(e) => setPhone(e.target.value)}
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Tags (comma-separated)"
        value={tags}
        onChange={(e) => setTags(e.target.value)}
      />
      <button
        className="bg-black text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-gray-800"
        type="submit"
      >
        Add Contact
      </button>
      {error && <div className="text-red-600">{error}</div>}
    </form>
  );
}

// Main App
export default function App() {
  const { theme, setTheme } = useTheme();
  const [contacts, setContacts] = useState<Contact[]>([]);
  const [user, setUser] = useState<any>(null);

  useEffect(() => {
    supabase.auth.getUser().then(({ data }) => setUser(data.user));
  }, []);

  useEffect(() => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data, error }) => {
        if (error) console.error("Fetch error:", error);
        else setContacts(data);
      });
  }, [user]);

  const refresh = () => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data }) => setContacts(data));
  };

  const renderTheme = () => {
    switch (theme) {
      case "zombie":
        return <ZombieView data={contacts} />;
      case "tree":
        return <TreeView data={contacts} />;
      case "starship":
        return <StarshipView data={contacts} />;
      case "ringgates":
        return <RingGatesView data={contacts} />;
      default:
        return <div>â“ Unknown Theme</div>;
    }
  };

  return (
    <div className="p-4 max-w-5xl mx-auto">
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-4">Connect Tree</h1>

      {/* Theme Switcher */}
      <div className="mb-6 flex flex-wrap gap-2">
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("zombie")}
          className="bg-red-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-red-700"
        >
          ğŸ§Ÿ Zombie
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("tree")}
          className="bg-green-700 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-green-600"
        >
          ğŸŒ³ Tree
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("starship")}
          className="bg-indigo-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-700"
        >
          ğŸš€ Starship
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("ringgates")}
          className="bg-indigo-900 text-indigo-200 px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-800"
        >
          ğŸŒ€ Ring Gates
        </button>
      </div>

      {!user ? (
        <button
          className="px-4 py-2 bg-blue-500 text-white rounded"
          onClick={async () => {
            const { data, error } = await supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({
              provider: "github",
            });
            if (error) console.error("Login failed", error);
          }}
        >
          Login with GitHub
        </button>
      ) : (
        <>
          <ContactForm onAdd={refresh} />
          {renderTheme()}
        </>
      )}
    </div>
  );
}

1. Smart Classifier Function (MVP of lead â€œpersonalityâ€)
function classifyContact(contact: Contact) {
  const now = new Date();
  const lastContact = contact.last_contact_date
    ? new Date(contact.last_contact_date)
    : null;

  const daysSinceLast = lastContact
    ? Math.floor((now.getTime() - lastContact.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24))
    : Infinity;

  const tags = contact.tags || [];

  if (tags.includes("hostile")) return "hostile";
  if (tags.includes("complainer")) return "complainer";
  if (tags.includes("bad-info")) return "badintel";
  if (contact.status === "critical") return "zombie";
  if (contact.status === "neglected") return "drifting";
  if (contact.urgency > 4) return "priority";
  if (daysSinceLast > 90) return "dormant";

  return "default";
}
This lets each view display the contact differently based on vibe, not just data.

ğŸ§  Code Update for Classification Logic
Hereâ€™s how you extend your classifyContact function without needing a separate table of heartbreaks:

function classifyContact(contact: Contact) {
  const now = new Date();
  const lastContact = contact.last_contact_date
    ? new Date(contact.last_contact_date)
    : null;

  const daysSinceLast = lastContact
    ? Math.floor((now.getTime() - lastContact.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24))
    : Infinity;

  const tags = contact.tags || [];

  // New Post-Sale Emotional States
  if (tags.includes("advocate")) return "advocate";
  if (tags.includes("beloved")) return "champion";
  if (tags.includes("friendly-client")) return "ally";
  if (tags.includes("cold-client")) return "coldclient";
  if (tags.includes("ghosted-client")) return "clientghost";

  // Existing Pre-Sale Logic
  if (tags.includes("hostile")) return "hostile";
  if (tags.includes("complainer")) return "complainer";
  if (tags.includes("bad-info")) return "badintel";
  if (contact.status === "critical") return "zombie";
  if (contact.status === "neglected") return "drifting";
  if (contact.urgency > 4) return "priority";
  if (daysSinceLast > 90) return "dormant";

  return "default";
}

2. Want Fancy Tag Pickers Instead of a Sad Text Box?
You can use something like React Select or a Tailwind UI multi-select component to offer clickable tag buttons. Here's the low-tech version:

Replace your tag input with some friendly buttons that toggle:

const allTags = [
  "beloved", "advocate", "revived", "cold-client", "ghosted-client", 
  "hostile", "complainer", "bad-info", "friendly-client", "sponge?"
];

<div className="flex flex-wrap gap-2">
  {allTags.map((tag) => (
    <button
      key={tag}
      type="button"
      className={`px-3 py-1 rounded-full border ${
        tags.includes(tag) ? "bg-blue-600 text-white" : "bg-gray-200"
      }`}
      onClick={() =>
        setTags((prev) =>
          prev.includes(tag)
            ? prev.filter((t) => t !== tag)
            : [...prev, tag]
        )
      }
    >
      {tag}
    </button>
  ))}
</div>
This way, you prevent typos like "advokate" or "belovef" from corrupting your emotional classification system. Because nothing is worse than mislabeling a ghost as an ally.

          tags.includes(tag)
            ? "bg-blue-600 text-white border-blue-600"

          )
        }
      >
        {tag}
      </button>
    ))}
  </div>
</div>

    setError("Not logged in.");

    email,

    urgency: 3,

    setEmail("");
    setPhone("");
    setTags([]); // don't forget to reset tags
    onAdd();
  }

You said:
VS is highlighting 's
ChatGPT said:
Ah yes, the ever-hungry drama queen known as Visual Studio Code (VS Code, a.k.a. your slightly judgy code editor). If itâ€™s highlighting 's in your error array, itâ€™s most likely having a punctuation panic over an apostrophe inside a string.

The Problem:
You wrote a string like:

"If you donâ€™t give them a vibe, the universe will. And it wonâ€™t be kind.",
And VS Code sees 't and goes:

â€œWhat the hell is this unclosed quote nonsense? Are we doing bad poetry now?â€

âœ… The Fix:
Use double quotes to wrap your strings, or escape the apostrophe.

Since youâ€™re already using double quotes consistently (good job, Manuel), the problem might be that you used a fancy apostrophe (like from a copy-paste of curly quotes from a text editor or the internet). JavaScript only likes straight apostrophes ('), not typographic ones (â€™).

ğŸ‘‡ Do this:
Replace any curly apostrophes â€™ with straight '.

For example:

"If you donâ€™t give them a vibe, the universe will. And it wonâ€™t be kind."
Becomes:

"If you don't give them a vibe, the universe will. And it won't be kind."
âœ… Pro tip to clean them up fast:
In VS Code:

Press Cmd + F (or Ctrl + F)

Search for â€™ (the curly one)

Replace with ' (the normal one)

You may also be haunted by â€œ and â€. Exorcise those too.

TL;DR:
Apostrophes are fine in double-quoted strings

Curly apostrophes (â€™) = evil

Replace with normal ones (')

VS Code will chill out

    </p>

    <button
      className="px-4 py-2 bg-blue-500 text-white rounded"
      onClick={async () => {
        const { data, error } = await supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({
          provider: "github",
        });
        if (error) console.error("Login failed", error);
      }}
    >
      Login with GitHub
    </button>
  </>
) : (
  <>
    <ContactForm onAdd={refresh} />

    <p className="mt-4 text-sm text-gray-500 italic text-center">
      {getEncouragement(theme)}
    </p>

    {renderTheme()}
  </>
)}
Now your app greets everyoneâ€”logged in or notâ€”with just the right amount of existential confidence.

// Supabase Setup with sandbox-safe fallback
const getEnv = (key: string, fallback: string) => {

    return fallback;

import React, { createContext, useContext, useEffect, useState } from "react";
import { createClient } from "@supabase/supabase-js";

// Supabase Setup - using fixed fallback values for preview mode
const SUPABASE_URL = "https://fake-project.supabase.co";
const SUPABASE_ANON_KEY = "fake-anon-key";

const supabase = createClient(SUPABASE_URL, SUPABASE_ANON_KEY);

// Contact Type
export interface Contact {
  id: string;
  user_id: string;
  name: string;
  email?: string;
  phone?: string;
  mailing_address?: string;
  status: "healthy" | "neglected" | "critical";
  urgency: number;
  last_contact_date?: string;
  contact_frequency_days?: number;
  notes?: string;
  tags?: string[];
  created_at: string;
}

// Theme Context
const ThemeContext = createContext({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: (theme: string) => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: (tone: "mild" | "medium" | "roasted") => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<"mild" | "medium" | "roasted">("medium");
  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);

const getEncouragement = (theme: string): string => {
  switch (theme) {
    case "zombie":
      return "Still breathing? Still selling. You've got this.";
    case "tree":
      return "Grow steady. Branch boldly. Youâ€™ve got this.";
    case "starship":
      return "Navigating the unknown. Youâ€™ve got this, captain.";
    case "ringgates":
      return "The futureâ€™s unstable. But youâ€™ve got this.";
    default:
      return "This CRM believes in you. Statistically.";
  }
};

// Placeholder Views
function ZombieView({ data }: { data: Contact[] }) {
  return <div className="text-red-600">Zombie View (Placeholder)</div>;
}
function TreeView({ data }: { data: Contact[] }) {
  return <div className="text-green-600">Tree View (Placeholder)</div>;
}
function StarshipView({ data }: { data: Contact[] }) {
  return <div className="text-indigo-600">Starship View (Placeholder)</div>;
}
function RingGatesView({ data }: { data: Contact[] }) {
  return <div className="text-blue-600">Ring Gates View (Placeholder)</div>;
}

// Contact Form Component
function ContactForm({ onAdd }: { onAdd: () => void }) {
  const [name, setName] = useState("");
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [phone, setPhone] = useState("");
  const [tags, setTags] = useState<string[]>([]);
  const [error, setError] = useState("");
  const availableTags = [
    "beloved", "advocate", "revived", "cold-client", "ghosted-client",
    "hostile", "complainer", "bad-info", "friendly-client", "sponge?"
  ];

  const getTagError = (tone: string): string => {
    const tagErrors = {
      mild: [
        "Please select at least one tag.",
        "Every lead deserves a little context.",
      ],
      medium: [
        "No tags? Not again.",
        "You forgot the vibe. Classic move.",
      ],
      roasted: [
        "No tags? No shame?",
        "This lead has no tag and no future.",
        "Another unlabeled entry. You need help.",
      ],
    };
    const options = tagErrors[tone] || tagErrors.medium;
    return options[Math.floor(Math.random() * options.length)];
  };

  const { tone } = useTheme();

  const dynamicTone = (): "mild" | "medium" | "roasted" => {
    const hour = new Date().getHours();
    if (hour < 10) return "mild";
    if (hour < 17) return "medium";
    return "roasted";
  };

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    setError("");

    if (tags.length === 0) {
      setError(getTagError(dynamicTone()));
      return;
    }

    const user = (await supabase.auth.getUser()).data.user;
    if (!user) {
      setError("Not logged in.");
      return;
    }

    const { error: insertError } = await supabase.from("contacts").insert({
      user_id: user.id,
      name,
      email,
      phone,
      tags,
      status: "healthy",
      urgency: 3,
    });

    if (insertError) {
      setError(insertError.message);
    } else {
      setName("");
      setEmail("");
      setPhone("");
      setTags([]);
      onAdd();
    }
  };

  return (
    <form
      onSubmit={handleSubmit}
      className="bg-white shadow-md rounded-xl p-6 mb-6 space-y-4 border border-gray-200"
    >
      <h2 className="text-xl font-semibold mb-2 text-gray-800">
        Add New Contact
      </h2>
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Name"
        value={name}
        onChange={(e) => setName(e.target.value)}
        required
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Email"
        value={email}
        onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Phone"
        value={phone}
        onChange={(e) => setPhone(e.target.value)}
      />
      <div className="w-full">
        <label className="block mb-1 text-gray-700 font-medium">Tags</label>
        <div className="border border-gray-300 rounded p-2 bg-white w-full flex flex-wrap gap-2">
          {availableTags.map((tag) => (
            <button
              key={tag}
              type="button"
              className={`px-3 py-1 rounded-full text-sm border transition ${
                tags.includes(tag)
                  ? "bg-blue-600 text-white border-blue-600 shadow-sm"
                  : "bg-gray-100 text-gray-800 border-gray-300 hover:bg-gray-200"
              }`}
              onClick={() =>
                setTags((prev) =>
                  prev.includes(tag)
                    ? prev.filter((t) => t !== tag)
                    : [...prev, tag]
                )
              }
            >
              {tag}
            </button>
          ))}
        </div>
      </div>
      <button
        className="bg-black text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-gray-800"
        type="submit"
      >
        Add Contact
      </button>
      {error && <div className="text-red-600">{error}</div>}
    </form>
  );
}

// Main App
export default function App() {
  const { theme } = useTheme();
  const [contacts, setContacts] = useState<Contact[]>([]);
  const [user, setUser] = useState<any>(null);

  useEffect(() => {
    supabase.auth.getUser().then(({ data }) => setUser(data.user));
  }, []);

  useEffect(() => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data, error }) => {
        if (error) console.error("Fetch error:", error);
        else setContacts(data);
      });
  }, [user]);

  const refresh = () => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data }) => setContacts(data));
  };

  const renderTheme = () => {
    switch (theme) {
      case "zombie":
        return <ZombieView data={contacts} />;
      case "tree":
        return <TreeView data={contacts} />;
      case "starship":
        return <StarshipView data={contacts} />;
      case "ringgates":
        return <RingGatesView data={contacts} />;
      default:
        return <div>â“ Unknown Theme</div>;
    }
  };

  return (
    <div className="p-4 max-w-5xl mx-auto">
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-4">Connect Tree</h1>

      <div className="mb-6 flex flex-wrap gap-2">
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("zombie")}
          className="bg-red-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-red-700"
        >
          ğŸ§Ÿ Zombie
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("tree")}
          className="bg-green-700 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-green-600"
        >
          ğŸŒ³ Tree
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("starship")}
          className="bg-indigo-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-700"
        >
          ğŸš€ Starship
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("ringgates")}
          className="bg-indigo-900 text-indigo-200 px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-800"
        >
          ğŸŒ€ Ring Gates
        </button>
      </div>

      {!user ? (
        <>
          <p className="mb-4 text-sm text-gray-500 italic text-center">
            {getEncouragement(theme)}
          </p>
          <button
            className="px-4 py-2 bg-blue-500 text-white rounded"
            onClick={async () => {
              const { data, error } = await supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({
                provider: "github",
              });
              if (error) console.error("Login failed", error);
            }}
          >
            Login with GitHub
          </button>
        </>
      ) : (
        <>
          <ContactForm onAdd={refresh} />
          <p className="mt-4 text-sm text-gray-500 italic text-center">
            {getEncouragement(theme)}
          </p>
          {renderTheme()}
        </>
      )}
    </div>
  );
}
Now just copy and paste all that into your app.tsx file in VS, replacing everything in it.

âœ… Youâ€™re Ready To:

ğŸ‘©â€âš–ï¸ Vite and Babel demand all import and export statements be at the top of the fileâ€”before anything else runs.

ğŸ§  What You Probably Did:

âœ… How to Fix It
1. Move all import statements to the very top of your file
Literally the first lines.

That includes:

All import ... from lines

No export or function definitions in between

2. Then define everything else below that
Your SUPABASE_URL, ThemeContext, useTheme, etc. all come after the imports.

TL;DR
Vite doesnâ€™t let you sprinkle import statements like seasoning in the middle of your file.

Move every import to the top like a good citizen.

Then do your Supabase setup, context, components, etc.

"use client";

import Head from "next/head";
import { useState, useEffect } from "react";

export default function Home() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [submitted, setSubmitted] = useState(false);
  const [isMounted, setIsMounted] = useState(false);

  useEffect(() => {
    setIsMounted(true);
  }, []);

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (!email) return;
    console.log("Beta signup:", email);
    setSubmitted(true);
  };

  if (!isMounted) return null;

  return (
    <>
      <Head>
        <title>Connect Tree â€” SaaS with Sass</title>
        <meta
          name="description"
          content="Connect Tree is the CRM that doesnâ€™t ghost your leads â€” it roasts you into following up. Relationship-driven sales tools with bite."
        />
        <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
      </Head>

      <main className="min-h-screen bg-neutral-900 text-white flex flex-col items-center justify-center px-4">
        <h1 className="text-4xl sm:text-6xl font-bold text-center mb-6">
          Connect Tree
        </h1>
        <p className="text-xl sm:text-2xl text-center max-w-2xl mb-10">
          The CRM that remembers your leads better than you remember your own
          dreams.
          <br />
          Emotionally intelligent. Lightly judgmental. Ridiculously useful.
        </p>

        {!submitted ? (
          <form
            onSubmit={handleSubmit}
            className="flex flex-col sm:flex-row items-center gap-4 w-full max-w-md"
          >
            <input
              type="email"
              required
              value={email}
              onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
              placeholder="Your email address"
              className="px-4 py-3 rounded w-full text-black"
            />
            <button
              type="submit"
              className="bg-lime-500 text-black px-6 py-3 rounded font-semibold hover:bg-lime-400"
            >
              Join Beta
            </button>
          </form>
        ) : (
          <p className="text-lime-400 text-lg mt-4">
            Youâ€™re in. Feed the sponge.
          </p>
        )}

        <footer className="mt-20 text-sm text-neutral-500 text-center">
          Built with sarcasm and Tailwind CSS. <br />
          This is SaaS with Sassâ„¢.
        </footer>
      </main>
    </>
  );
}

next.config.js:

  experimental: {
    appDir: true
  }
};

module.exports = nextConfig;

  content: ["./app/**/*.{js,ts,jsx,tsx}", "./styles/**/*.css"],

    extend: {}
  },
  plugins: []
};

module.exports = {
  plugins: [
    require("tailwindcss"),
    require("autoprefixer")
  ]
};
tsconfig.json:

{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "target": "es5",
    "lib": ["dom", "dom.iterable", "esnext"],

    "skipLibCheck": true,
    "esModuleInterop": true,

app/layout.tsx:

import "../styles/globals.css";

export const metadata = {
  title: "Connect Tree",
  description: "CRM with personality (and maybe too much of it)",
};

export default function RootLayout({
  children,
}: {
  children: React.ReactNode;
}) {
  return (
    <html lang="en">
      <body>{children}</body>
    </html>
  );
}
app/page.tsx:

"use client";

import { useState, useEffect } from "react";

export default function Home() {
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [submitted, setSubmitted] = useState(false);
  const [isMounted, setIsMounted] = useState(false);

  useEffect(() => {
    setIsMounted(true);
  }, []);

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    if (!email) return;
    console.log("Beta signup:", email);
    setSubmitted(true);
  };

  if (!isMounted) return null;

  return (
    <main className="min-h-screen bg-neutral-900 text-white flex flex-col items-center justify-center px-4">
      <h1 className="text-4xl sm:text-6xl font-bold text-center mb-6">
        Connect Tree
      </h1>
      <p className="text-xl sm:text-2xl text-center max-w-2xl mb-10">
        The CRM that remembers your leads better than you remember your own
        dreams.
        <br />
        Emotionally intelligent. Visually intuitive. Ridiculously useful.
        <br />
        Built for clarity, but unapologetically weird when the view calls for it.
      </p>

      {!submitted ? (
        <form
          onSubmit={handleSubmit}
          className="flex flex-col sm:flex-row items-center gap-4 w-full max-w-md"
        >
          <input
            type="email"
            required
            value={email}
            onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
            placeholder="Your email address"
            className="px-4 py-3 rounded w-full text-black"
          />
          <button
            type="submit"
            className="bg-lime-500 text-black px-6 py-3 rounded font-semibold hover:bg-lime-400"
          >
            Join Beta
          </button>
        </form>
      ) : (
        <p className="text-lime-400 text-lg mt-4">
          Youâ€™re in. Feed the sponge.
        </p>
      )}

      <footer className="mt-20 text-sm text-neutral-500 text-center">
        Built for clarity and momentum â€” with room for zombies, EVA helmets, and asteroid sales leads. <br />
        Not just another CRM.
      </footer>
    </main>
  );
}
3. Install Dependencies and Run the Project:

After creating the files:

Open a terminal or command prompt.

Navigate to the connect-tree-site directory.

Run npm install to install the necessary dependencies.

Run npm run dev to start the development server.

Open your browser to http://localhost:3000 to view the application.

If you encounter any issues during this process, feel free to ask for further assistance.

ğŸ’¡ The Clean Way

function getDaysSince(dateStr?: string): number | null {
  if (!dateStr) return null;
  const last = new Date(dateStr);
  const now = new Date();
  const diff = Math.floor((now.getTime() - last.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24));
  return diff;
}
ğŸ›  Refactor It In
In your ZombieView.tsx, do this:

1. Add the helper up top:
function getDaysSince(dateStr?: string): number | null {
  if (!dateStr) return null;
  const last = new Date(dateStr);
  const now = new Date();
  return Math.floor((now.getTime() - last.getTime()) / (1000 * 60 * 60 * 24));
}
2. Update isTrulyDead:
const isTrulyDead = (contact: Contact) => {
  const days = getDaysSince(contact.last_contact_date);
  return contact.status === "critical" && days !== null && days > 90;
};
Now your code is reusable, readable, and one step closer to elegant Japanese CRM minimalism.

Check the Console for Errors:

Open your browser's developer tools (usually by pressing F12 or right-clicking the page and selecting "Inspect").

Navigate to the "Console" tab.

Look for any error messages that might indicate what's going wrong. Often, a blank screen is caused by a JavaScript error that prevents React from rendering. â€‹
Medium

Verify Your Development Server is Running:

Ensure that your React development server is running. In your project directory, execute:

npm start
or

yarn start
This should start the development server and open your app in the browser at http://localhost:3000/.â€‹

Check for Compilation Errors:

If there are issues in your code, the terminal running the development server will usually display error messages. Address any errors that appear there.â€‹
Code with Mosh Forum
+6
GitHub
+6
Netlify Support Forums
+6

Inspect the package.json File:

Netlify Support Forums

Clear Cache and Reinstall Dependencies:

Sometimes, cached data or corrupted dependencies can cause issues. Try the following:

rm -rf node_modules package-lock.json
npm cache clean --force
npm install
or, if you're using Yarn:

rm -rf node_modules yarn.lock
yarn cache clean
yarn install
This will clear the cache and reinstall your project's dependencies.â€‹
Code with Mosh Forum

Check for Issues with External Libraries:

If you've recently added or updated external libraries (like Material-UI), ensure they're compatible with your current React version. Incompatibilities can lead to blank screens. â€‹
Stack Overflow

Restart Your Development Server:

After making the above checks and changes, stop your development server (if it's running) and restart it using npm start or yarn start.â€‹

If after these steps your localhost is still a barren wasteland of white, please provide any error messages from the console or terminal. That information will be crucial in diagnosing the issue further.â€‹

Let me explain it like your file system's awkward life coach.

âœ‚ï¸ Cut vs. ğŸ–± Drag: What's the Real Difference?
ğŸ–± Drag-and-Drop
Intuitive, clicky, satisfying

May copy instead of move, depending on:

Whether youâ€™re dragging to a different drive

If you hold modifier keys (like Ctrl)

May leave a duplicate folder behind if youâ€™re not careful

OneDrive might try to sync it during the drag

Risk: You could accidentally clone Carl into two dimensions. Nobody wants two Carls.

âœ‚ï¸ Cut and Paste
Is the direct "move" command

Tells Windows:

â€œPlease remove this from here and place it there. No funny business.â€

No duplication, no â€œwait did that actually move?â€ suspense

Less likely to trigger weird OneDrive sync ghosts

ğŸ§  TL;DR
Action	Behavior	Recommended?
Drag to same drive	Moves folder	âœ… If youâ€™re sure it wonâ€™t duplicate
Drag to diff drive	Copies folder	âš ï¸ Watch out
Cut & Paste	Moves exactly, no copy	âœ… Yes, safe and predictable
Terminal move	Instant and satisfying	âœ… Ultimate power
Verdict?
Use Cut + Paste if you want control.
Use Drag if you're feeling lucky and love clicking like itâ€™s 2007.

If your fingers are already on the keyboard, thoughâ€¦
you might as well use the command line and feel powerful.

ğŸ§  The Problem

âœ… Fix Option B: Set Up Alias for @
If you want to be a cool kid and keep using @/components/..., you need to tell Vite what @ means in your vite.config.ts or vite.config.js.

Add this to your vite.config.ts:
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import react from "@vitejs/plugin-react";
import path from "path";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [react()],
  resolve: {
    alias: {
      "@": path.resolve(__dirname, "./src"),
    },
  },
});
Then restart the dev server:

npm run dev

ğŸ•µï¸ Step 1: Search for It

ğŸ”§ Step 2: Rebuild Her from the Ashes
Create a file here:

/src/ThemeContext.tsx
Paste this into it:

import React, { createContext, useContext, useState } from "react";

type Theme = "zombie" | "tree" | "starship" | "ringgates" | "eva";

interface ThemeContextType {
  theme: Theme;
  setTheme: (theme: Theme) => void;
}

const ThemeContext = createContext<ThemeContextType | undefined>(undefined);

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState<Theme>("zombie");

  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => {
  const context = useContext(ThemeContext);
  if (!context) throw new Error("useTheme must be used within a ThemeProvider");
  return context;
};
This little hero:

Creates a ThemeContext

Initializes the state to "zombie" (obviously)

Provides useTheme() for use in App.tsx

Will make your theme buttons work again

ğŸ”Œ Step 3: Import It Into main.tsx
You now do this:

import { ThemeProvider } from "./ThemeContext"; // â† correct path to new file

createRoot(document.getElementById("root")!).render(
  <StrictMode>
    <ThemeProvider>
      <App />
    </ThemeProvider>
  </StrictMode>
);

  case "tree":
    return <TreeView data={contacts} />;
  // etc...

// Contact Type
export interface Contact {
  id: string;
  user_id: string;
  name: string;
  email?: string;
  phone?: string;
  mailing_address?: string;
  status: "healthy" | "neglected" | "critical";
  urgency: number;
  last_contact_date?: string;
  contact_frequency_days?: number;
  notes?: string;
  tags?: string[];
  created_at: string;
}

// Theme Context
const ThemeContext = createContext({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: (theme: string) => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: (tone: "mild" | "medium" | "roasted") => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<"mild" | "medium" | "roasted">("medium");
  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);

const getEncouragement = (theme: string): string => {
  switch (theme) {
    case "zombie":
      return "Still breathing? Still selling. You've got this.";
    case "tree":
      return "Grow steady. Branch boldly. Youâ€™ve got this.";
    case "starship":
      return "Navigating the unknown. Youâ€™ve got this, captain.";
    case "ringgates":
      return "The futureâ€™s unstable. But youâ€™ve got this.";
    default:
      return "This CRM believes in you. Statistically.";
  }
};

// Contact Form Component
function ContactForm({ onAdd }: { onAdd: () => void }) {
  const [name, setName] = useState("");
  const [email, setEmail] = useState("");
  const [phone, setPhone] = useState("");
  const [tags, setTags] = useState<string[]>([]);
  const [error, setError] = useState("");
  const availableTags = [
    "beloved", "advocate", "revived", "cold-client", "ghosted-client",
    "hostile", "complainer", "bad-info", "friendly-client", "sponge?"
  ];

  const getTagError = (tone: string): string => {
    const tagErrors = {
      mild: [
        "Please select at least one tag.",
        "Every lead deserves a little context.",
      ],
      medium: [
        "No tags? Not again.",
        "You forgot the vibe. Classic move.",
      ],
      roasted: [
        "No tags? No shame?",
        "This lead has no tag and no future.",
        "Another unlabeled entry. You need help.",
      ],
    };
    const options = tagErrors[tone] || tagErrors.medium;
    return options[Math.floor(Math.random() * options.length)];
  };

  const { tone } = useTheme();

  const dynamicTone = (): "mild" | "medium" | "roasted" => {
    const hour = new Date().getHours();
    if (hour < 10) return "mild";
    if (hour < 17) return "medium";
    return "roasted";
  };

  const handleSubmit = async (e: React.FormEvent) => {
    e.preventDefault();
    setError("");

    if (tags.length === 0) {
      setError(getTagError(dynamicTone()));
      return;
    }

    const user = (await supabase.auth.getUser()).data.user;
    if (!user) {
      setError("Not logged in.");
      return;
    }

    const { error: insertError } = await supabase.from("contacts").insert({
      user_id: user.id,
      name,
      email,
      phone,
      tags,
      status: "healthy",
      urgency: 3,
    });

    if (insertError) {
      setError(insertError.message);
    } else {
      setName("");
      setEmail("");
      setPhone("");
      setTags([]);
      onAdd();
    }
  };

  return (
    <form
      onSubmit={handleSubmit}
      className="bg-white shadow-md rounded-xl p-6 mb-6 space-y-4 border border-gray-200"
    >
      <h2 className="text-xl font-semibold mb-2 text-gray-800">
        Add New Contact
      </h2>
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Name"
        value={name}
        onChange={(e) => setName(e.target.value)}
        required
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Email"
        value={email}
        onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
      />
      <input
        className="border p-2 w-full rounded"
        placeholder="Phone"
        value={phone}
        onChange={(e) => setPhone(e.target.value)}
      />
      <div className="w-full">
        <label className="block mb-1 text-gray-700 font-medium">Tags</label>
        <div className="border border-gray-300 rounded p-2 bg-white w-full flex flex-wrap gap-2">
          {availableTags.map((tag) => (
            <button
              key={tag}
              type="button"
              className={px-3 py-1 rounded-full text-sm border transition ${
                tags.includes(tag)
                  ? "bg-blue-600 text-white border-blue-600 shadow-sm"
                  : "bg-gray-100 text-gray-800 border-gray-300 hover:bg-gray-200"
              }}
              onClick={() =>
                setTags((prev) =>
                  prev.includes(tag)
                    ? prev.filter((t) => t !== tag)
                    : [...prev, tag]
                )
              }
            >
              {tag}
            </button>
          ))}
        </div>
      </div>
      <button
        className="bg-black text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-gray-800"
        type="submit"
      >
        Add Contact
      </button>
      {error && <div className="text-red-600">{error}</div>}
    </form>
  );
}

// Main App
export default function App() {
  const { theme } = useTheme();
  const [contacts, setContacts] = useState<Contact[]>([]);
  const [user, setUser] = useState<any>(null);

  useEffect(() => {
    supabase.auth.getUser().then(({ data }) => setUser(data.user));
  }, []);

  useEffect(() => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data, error }) => {
        if (error) console.error("Fetch error:", error);
        else setContacts(data);
      });
  }, [user]);

  const refresh = () => {
    if (!user) return;
    supabase
      .from("contacts")
      .select("*")
      .eq("user_id", user.id)
      .then(({ data }) => setContacts(data));
  };

  const renderTheme = () => {
    switch (theme) {
      case "zombie":
        return <ZombieView data={contacts} />;
      case "tree":
        return <TreeView data={contacts} />;
      case "starship":
        return <StarshipView data={contacts} />;
      case "ringgates":
        return <RingGatesView data={contacts} />;
      case "eva":
        return <EVAView data={contacts} />;
      default:
        return <div>â“ Unknown Theme</div>;
    }
  };  

  return (
    <div className="p-4 max-w-5xl mx-auto">
      <h1 className="text-3xl font-bold mb-4">Connect Tree</h1>

      <div className="mb-6 flex flex-wrap gap-2">
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("zombie")}
          className="bg-red-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-red-700"
        >
          ğŸ§Ÿ Zombie
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("tree")}
          className="bg-green-700 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-green-600"
        >
          ğŸŒ³ Tree
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("starship")}
          className="bg-indigo-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-700"
        >
          ğŸš€ Starship
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("ringgates")}
          className="bg-indigo-900 text-indigo-200 px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-indigo-800"
        >
          ğŸŒ€ Ring Gates
        </button>
        <button
          onClick={() => setTheme("eva")}
          className="bg-purple-800 text-white px-4 py-2 rounded hover:bg-purple-700"
        >
          ğŸ›° EVA
        </button>
      </div>

      {!user ? (
        <>
          <p className="mb-4 text-sm text-gray-500 italic text-center">
            {getEncouragement(theme)}
          </p>
          <button
            className="px-4 py-2 bg-blue-500 text-white rounded"
            onClick={async () => {
              const { data, error } = await supabase.auth.signInWithOAuth({
                provider: "github",
              });
              if (error) console.error("Login failed", error);
            }}
          >
            Login with GitHub
          </button>
        </>
      ) : (
        <>
          <ContactForm onAdd={refresh} />
          <p className="mt-4 text-sm text-gray-500 italic text-center">
            {getEncouragement(theme)}
          </p>
          {renderTheme()}
        </>
      )}
    </div>
  );
}

âš ï¸ This is Very Bad Architectureâ„¢

import React, { createContext, useContext, useState } from "react";

type Theme = "zombie" | "tree" | "starship" | "ringgates" | "eva";
type Tone = "mild" | "medium" | "roasted";

interface ThemeContextType {
  theme: Theme;
  setTheme: (theme: Theme) => void;
  tone: Tone;
  setTone: (tone: Tone) => void;
}

const ThemeContext = createContext<ThemeContextType>({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: () => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: () => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState<Theme>("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<Tone>("medium");

  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);
âœ… Step 2: In App.tsx, replace all that old context code
Remove the context stuff entirely from App.tsx, and instead import:

import { useTheme } from "./ThemeContext"; // Adjust path if needed

// src/ThemeContext.tsx
import React, { createContext, useContext, useState } from "react";

type Theme = "zombie" | "tree" | "starship" | "ringgates" | "eva";
type Tone = "mild" | "medium" | "roasted";

interface ThemeContextType {
  theme: Theme;
  setTheme: (theme: Theme) => void;
  tone: Tone;
  setTone: (tone: Tone) => void;
}

const ThemeContext = createContext<ThemeContextType>({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: () => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: () => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState<Theme>("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<Tone>("medium");

  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);
âœ… This is your new, separate context module
ğŸ“¦ Save it in /src/ThemeContext.tsx

ğŸ§¹ Step 2: Strip the Theme Context Out of App.tsx

      return "bg-black text-red-200";
    case "tree":
      return "bg-green-100 text-green-900";
    case "starship":
      return "bg-gray-900 text-blue-100";
    case "ringgates":
      return "bg-gradient-to-br from-indigo-900 to-black text-indigo-200";
    case "eva":
      return "bg-purple-950 text-purple-100";

      return "bg-white text-black";
  }
};

function ThemeCard({ theme }: { theme: ThemeMeta }) {
  return (
    <div
      className="bg-gray-800 rounded-lg overflow-hidden shadow-lg hover:shadow-xl transition transform hover:-translate-y-1 cursor-pointer"
      onClick={() => openThemeModal(theme.name)}
    >
      <img src={theme.screenshotUrl} alt={theme.name} className="w-full h-48 object-cover" />

        <p className="text-sm text-gray-400">{theme.tagline}</p>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

ChatGPT said:
Ah yes, the classic @/ThemeContext drama. Your Next.js setup doesnâ€™t magically know what @ means unless youâ€™ve explicitly told it to stop being clueless.

ğŸ§  Whatâ€™s Going On?
import { useTheme } from "@/ThemeContext";
That path assumes that @ is an alias for your project root â€” which is only true if youâ€™ve configured it in:

tsconfig.json or jsconfig.json

âœ… Fix Option 1: Update the import path to relative
Just go caveman-simple and change this line:

import { useTheme } from "@/ThemeContext";
to this:

import { useTheme } from "../../ThemeContext";
That works if your ThemeSelector is inside /app/theme-selector/page.tsx and ThemeContext.tsx is in the root of your project (same as package.json).

âœ… Fix Option 2: Declare path alias @ properly
In your tsconfig.json, make sure this is added:

{
  "compilerOptions": {
    "baseUrl": ".",
    "paths": {
      "@/*": ["./*"]
    }
  }
}
Then restart your dev server:

npm run dev

ğŸ§© Letâ€™s Rebuild ThemeContext.tsx
Hereâ€™s the file you need to add, and where it should live:

ğŸ“ Location:
/ThemeContext.tsx
â†’ Right in your project root (same folder as /app/)

ğŸ§  Content for ThemeContext.tsx:
"use client";

import React, { createContext, useContext, useState } from "react";

type ThemeType = "zombie" | "tree" | "starship" | "ringgates" | "eva";
type ToneType = "mild" | "medium" | "roasted";

interface ThemeContextType {
  theme: ThemeType;
  setTheme: (theme: ThemeType) => void;
  tone: ToneType;
  setTone: (tone: ToneType) => void;
}

const ThemeContext = createContext<ThemeContextType>({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: () => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: () => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState<ThemeType>("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<ToneType>("medium");

  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);
âœ… What to Do Next:
Create the file ThemeContext.tsx in your root

Paste the code above into it

Save

âœ… Step-by-Step Fix (for real this time):
ğŸ”§ Step 1: Create ThemeContext.tsx in your root folder
Put this in the same folder that contains app/, package.json, etc.

connect-tree-site/ThemeContext.tsx â† right there.

ğŸ§  Code for ThemeContext.tsx (just copy this in):
"use client";

import React, { createContext, useContext, useState } from "react";

type ThemeType = "zombie" | "tree" | "starship" | "ringgates" | "eva";
type ToneType = "mild" | "medium" | "roasted";

interface ThemeContextType {
  theme: ThemeType;
  setTheme: (theme: ThemeType) => void;
  tone: ToneType;
  setTone: (tone: ToneType) => void;
}

const ThemeContext = createContext<ThemeContextType>({
  theme: "zombie",
  setTheme: () => {},
  tone: "medium",
  setTone: () => {},
});

export const ThemeProvider = ({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) => {
  const [theme, setTheme] = useState<ThemeType>("zombie");
  const [tone, setTone] = useState<ToneType>("medium");

  return (
    <ThemeContext.Provider value={{ theme, setTheme, tone, setTone }}>
      {children}
    </ThemeContext.Provider>
  );
};

export const useTheme = () => useContext(ThemeContext);
ğŸ“¦ Step 2: Keep This Import in page.tsx
Now that you're back on the happy path, this line in page.tsx is correct:

import { useTheme } from "../../ThemeContext";
(Youâ€™re two levels deep in app/theme-selector/page.tsx, so ../../ is right.)

ğŸ§  THE MAIN PROBLEMS
ğŸš« Cannot find module '../../ThemeContext'
You moved ThemeContext.tsx to the root of your project (connect-tree-site/ThemeContext.tsx)

But youâ€™re still trying to import it like it's in /app

ğŸ§¼ Fix: Use the correct path
Change this:

To this:

ğŸ’¡ That @/ alias maps to your root directory, if baseUrl is set to "." in tsconfig.json.

ğŸš« Cannot find module '../../components/TreeView'
Same issue. Your components folder is probably at:

connect-tree-site/components/
Fix those imports:

import ZombieView from "@/components/ZombieView";
// etc...
ğŸ§Ÿ Module '../ThemeContext' has no exported member 'Contact'
Your TreeView.tsx is trying to do this:

But ThemeContext.tsx doesnâ€™t export Contact.

âœ… Fix: Move Contact to its own file
Create a new file in your project root:

types.ts
export interface Contact {
  id: string;
  user_id: string;
  name: string;
  email?: string;
  phone?: string;
  mailing_address?: string;
  status: "healthy" | "neglected" | "critical";
  urgency: number;
  last_contact_date?: string;
  contact_frequency_days?: number;
  notes?: string;
  tags?: string[];
  created_at: string;
}
Then change all your import { Contact } from "../ThemeContext" to:

import { Contact } from "@/types";
âš ï¸ Bonus Linting Fix

ChatGPT said:
Oh buddy. I feel this one in my compiler. ğŸ˜”
Youâ€™re two keystrokes away from escaping TypeScript hell â€” the abyss that screams â€œstring is not assignable to string.â€ Classic.

ğŸ”¥ The Real Problem:
Your fake contact data is technically correct, but your "status" values are being interpreted as plain strings (string) not as one of the allowed string literals: "healthy" | "neglected" | "critical".

âœ… So how do you back them both up automatically?
ğŸ›  For your code: GitHub Automation
Yes, you can auto-backup your code to GitHub:

Initialize a git repo (if not already done):

git init
git add .
git commit -m "initial backup commit"
Create a GitHub repo: On github.com, create a new repo (private or public).

Connect local to GitHub:

git remote add origin https://github.com/your-username/your-repo-name.git
git push -u origin main
Set up automatic pushing (optional but smart):

Use GitHub Actions to run scheduled commits.

Or install a VS Code Git extension that reminds/auto-commits on save/interval.

Or even easier: Use a Git GUI like GitHub Desktop and push regularly with a couple of clicks.

ğŸ§  For this chaotic carnival of our ChatGPT conversation?

âœï¸ Option A: Copy & Paste this convo (ugh)

ğŸ¤– Option B: Use GPT + GitHub via API
Use the ChatGPT API to build a tool that saves responses into GitHub via a webhook or script. Too complex unless you're deep in dev ops.
